Let me first check if there's a way to run just the braveadblock tests locally.\n\nActually, based on my analysis of the code, I understand the bug now. Let me trace through the logic:\n\nIn `read_cache()`:\n```python\ndef read_cache(self) -> None:\n    \"\"\"Initialize the adblocking engine from cache file.\"\"\"\n    try:\n        cache_exists = self._cache_path.is_file()\n    except OSError:\n        logger.error(\"Failed to read adblock cache\", exc_info=True)\n        return\n\n    if cache_exists:\n        logger.debug(\"Loading cached adblock data: %s\", self._cache_path)\n        try:\n            with _map_exceptions():\n                self._engine.deserialize_from_file(str(self._cache_path))\n        except DeserializationError as e:\n            message.error(\"Reading adblock filter data failed (corrupted data?). \"\n                          \"Please run :adblock-update.\")\n```\n\nAnd in `_map_exceptions()`:\n```python\nadblock_deserialization_error = getattr(\n    adblock, \"DeserializationError\", ValueError)\n\ntry:\n    yield\nexcept adblock_deserialization_error as e:\n    if isinstance(e, ValueError) and str(e) != \"DeserializationError\":\n        # All Rust exceptions get turned into a ValueError by\n        # python-adblock\n        raise\n    raise DeserializationError(str(e))\n```\n\nThe problem is:\n1. If the adblock version is >= 0.5.0, `adblock_deserialization_error` is `adblock.DeserializationError`\n2. If the adblock version is < 0.5.0, `adblock_deserialization_error` is `ValueError`\n3. But in older versions, if a `ValueError` is raised during deserialization, how do we know if it's a deserialization error or some other error?\n\n\n4. The check `if isinstance(e, ValueError) and str(e) != \"DeserializationError\": raise` only re-raises if the message doesn't match, otherwise it converts to `DeserializationError`. However, in newer versions with the actual `DeserializationError` class, any other exception type won't be caught by this handler and will propagate uncaught. The logic assumes only deserialization errors will be raised, but doesn't account for other potential exceptions from the deserialization process.\n\nLooking at the existing test for corrupt cache handling, it writes invalid data and expects the error to be caught and logged. If the application was crashing on corrupted cache, that test would already be failing. So the issue might be more subtle—perhaps certain types of corruption trigger different exceptions that bypass the current error handling entirely.\n\nThe task description emphasizes that the crash happens during startup initialization, not when `read_cache()` is called directly. This suggests the problem occurs in the `init()` function specifically, where an exception from the adblock library isn't being caught before it propagates to the application level. The deserialization error escapes as an unhandled exception, preventing the browser window from even appearing.\n\nLooking at the `init()` function, it instantiates `BraveAdBlocker` and immediately calls `read_cache()` without any exception handling around that call. Even though `read_cache()` has internal try/except blocks for certain operations like checking if the cache file exists, those blocks don't cover all possible failure points—particularly the actual deserialization of corrupted cache data.\n\nThe `except DeserializationError` handler catches that specific error and shows a user message, but if a different exception type gets raised during deserialization, it would propagate up uncaught since `init()` has no wrapper around the `read_cache()` call. This could crash the initialization process entirely. :\n\n```python\nadblock_deserialization_error = getattr(\n    adblock, \"DeserializationError\", ValueError)\n\ntry:\n    yield\nexcept adblock_deserialization_error as e:\n    ...\n```\n\nIf the adblock library raises an exception type other than `DeserializationError`, it won't be caught by this handler.
